💬 Response (12,416 in / 609 out)
Here is what you need to know.

## What happens after you apply

The Home Office will check your application and send you a certificate of application by email or post. This certificate lets you prove your right to work, rent, use the NHS, and claim benefits while you wait for a decision.

When a decision is made, you will get a decision letter by email or post. Your eVisa will then be updated in your UKVI account.

## How to check your application

There is no online tracker for EU Settlement Scheme applications. The best ways to check progress are:

- Sign in to your [UKVI account](https://www.gov.uk/evisa) to see if your eVisa has been updated
- Check your email inbox, including your junk or spam folder, for any messages from the Home Office
- Contact the Home Office directly if you have heard nothing and are concerned

## How long it takes

Most applications are straightforward and decided quickly, but some can take longer if the Home Office needs more information. If they do need more from you, they will contact you before making a decision.

## If you need to prove your status while you wait

You can use your certificate of application to prove your rights in the meantime. You can also get a share code from your [UKVI account](https://www.gov.uk/evisa) to show employers or landlords.

For full details, see [what happens after you apply on GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/settled-status-eu-citizens-families/after-youve-applied).

💬 Response (7,464 in / 437 out)
Here is how to check on your application.

## Check your eVisa account first

The quickest way to check is to sign in to your UKVI account. If your settled status has been granted, it will show there.

- Sign in and view your status at gov.uk/view-prove-immigration-status
- If it shows settled status, your application has been approved

## If it has not been updated yet

Your application may still be under review. Processing times can vary.

- Check your email (including your spam folder) for any correspondence from the Home Office
- Make sure your UKVI account details are up to date so you do not miss a notification

## Contact the Home Office directly

If you have been waiting a long time and have heard nothing, you can contact UK Visas and Immigration.

1. Go to gov.uk/contact-ukvi-inside-outside-uk
2. Select "Inside the UK"
3. Select "Settled or pre-settled status (EU Settlement Scheme)"
4. Follow the steps to reach the right contact option — webchat is usually the fastest

## While you wait

Your existing pre-settled status remains valid while your application is being processed. You can still work, rent, and access services as normal. You do not need to do anything else right now.

💬 Response (21,891 in / 1,206 out)
Here is what you need to do and what support is available to you.

## Telling DVLA about your diagnosis

You must tell the DVLA that you have Parkinson's disease. This is a legal requirement. If you do not, you can be fined up to £1,000. You could also be prosecuted if you are involved in an accident.

1. Report your condition to the DVLA online at [Parkinson's disease and driving - GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/parkinsons-disease-and-driving)
2. Or fill in form PK1 (for a car or motorcycle licence) and post it to the DVLA - the address is on the form
3. If you hold a bus, coach or lorry licence, fill in form PK1V instead

The DVLA will then decide whether you can continue to drive. They may issue you a short-term licence so your driving can be reviewed regularly.

## Financial support

You may be able to claim benefits to help with extra costs.

- Personal Independence Payment (PIP) - helps with daily living and getting around. You can claim this even if you are working. [Apply for PIP on GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/pip)
- Attendance Allowance - if you are State Pension age or over and need help with personal care
- Universal Credit - if you are on a low income or out of work. [Find out about Universal Credit](https://www.gov.uk/universal-credit)

If you live in Scotland, apply for Adult Disability Payment (ADP) instead of PIP.

## Help with transport and getting around

- Blue Badge - lets you park closer to where you need to go. [Apply for a Blue Badge](https://www.gov.uk/apply-blue-badge)
- Disabled Persons Railcard - reduces the cost of train travel
- Motability Scheme - helps you buy or lease a car using your PIP mobility payment
- Disabled persons bus pass - free or reduced bus travel in your area

## Help at home

- Disabled Facilities Grant - money from your local council to adapt your home
- Direct payments - lets you arrange your own care and support

## Help at work

- Access to Work grant - pays for equipment, support workers or help getting to work. [Find out about Access to Work](https://www.gov.uk/access-to-work)

You can see a full overview of all disability-related financial support at [Financial help if you're disabled - GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/financial-help-disabled).

Start by telling the DVLA about your diagnosis, then apply for PIP, as a successful PIP award can open the door to other support such as the Blue Badge and Motability Scheme.

💬 Response (31,311 in / 1,066 out)
Here is a full guide to what you need to do and what support is available.

## Your legal duty — tell DVLA now

This is the most urgent step. You must tell DVLA about your Parkinson's diagnosis. You can be fined up to £1,000 if you do not, and your insurance could be invalid.

1. Report your condition online at [Parkinson's disease and driving on GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/parkinsons-disease-and-driving), or fill in form PK1 and post it to DVLA
2. DVLA will write to you and may ask for more information from your doctor
3. DVLA will then decide whether you can keep your licence, need a shorter-term licence, or must stop driving

## Financial support you can apply for

Once you have notified DVLA, look at these benefits and entitlements.

- Personal Independence Payment (PIP) — for people under 65. Covers daily living and mobility needs. Not means-tested. [Apply for PIP](https://www.gov.uk/pip)
- Attendance Allowance — if you are 65 or over and need help with personal care. [Apply for Attendance Allowance](https://www.gov.uk/attendance-allowance)
- Free NHS prescriptions — you may qualify if you receive PIP or another qualifying benefit. [Check eligibility](https://www.gov.uk/get-free-prescriptions-on-the-nhs)
- Council Tax Disability Reduction — if your home has adaptations for your condition. [Apply via your local council](https://www.gov.uk/council-tax/discounts-for-disabled-people)

## If you receive PIP mobility component (enhanced rate)

These extra entitlements open up once you have a PIP award at the enhanced mobility rate.

- Blue Badge — lets you park in disabled bays. [Apply via your local council](https://www.gov.uk/apply-blue-badge)
- Vehicle Excise Duty (road tax) exemption — your vehicle tax becomes free. [Find out more](https://www.gov.uk/financial-help-disabled/vehicles-and-transport)
- Motability scheme — lease a car or scooter using your mobility component. [Find out more at Motability](https://www.motability.co.uk/)

## If you are still working

- Access to Work — grants for workplace adaptations, travel costs, or a support worker. [Apply for Access to Work](https://www.gov.uk/access-to-work)

## Help at home

- Care needs assessment — your local authority will assess what support you need and may fund it. Free to request. [Request a care needs assessment](https://www.gov.uk/care-needs-assessment-adults)
- Disabled Facilities Grant — up to £30,000 for home adaptations such as ramps or stairlifts. Requires a care assessment first. [Find out more](https://www.gov.uk/disabled-facilities-grants)

## Disabled Persons Railcard

If you receive PIP or Attendance Allowance, you qualify for a [Disabled Persons Railcard](https://www.disabledpersons-railcard.co.uk/) — one third off most rail fares for you and a companion. It costs £20 a year.

---

Start by reporting your condition to DVLA straight away at [gov.uk/parkinsons-disease-and-driving](https://www.gov.uk/parkinsons-disease-and-driving), then apply for PIP (or Attendance Allowance if you are 65 or over) as this unlocks many of the other entitlements above.
⚖️ Judge scores — Completeness: 5/5 · Accuracy: 4/5 · Sequencing: 5/5 · Clarity: 5/5
Completeness 5/5 ●●●●●
All essential services (DVLA notification, PIP) are covered, all conditional services (VED exemption, Motability, Blue Badge, NHS care assessment) are included, and proactive services (Council Tax Disability Reduction, Attendance Allowance) are volunteered, plus additional relevant services like Access to Work, Disabled Facilities Grant, and Disabled Persons Railcard.
Accuracy 4/5 ●●●●○
Minor imprecision: PIP is described as 'for people under 65' when in fact it is for people under State Pension age (which can differ) and those already receiving it can continue past that age; also free NHS prescriptions eligibility is more nuanced than stated, as PIP itself does not automatically qualify someone for free prescriptions (it depends on other factors like income-related benefits or medical exemption certificates).
Sequencing 5/5 ●●●●●
The response correctly prioritises the legal duty to notify DVLA as the most urgent step, then positions PIP/Attendance Allowance as the key gateway benefit, and clearly explains that Blue Badge, VED exemption, and Motability are contingent on enhanced rate PIP mobility — dependencies are well communicated.
Clarity 5/5 ●●●●●
Exceptionally well-structured with clear headings, logical groupings, appropriate use of links, and a concise summary at the end reinforcing the priority actions; the depth is appropriate without being overwhelming.
Notable errors: PIP age threshold described as 'under 65' rather than 'under State Pension age', Free NHS prescriptions eligibility oversimplified — PIP receipt alone does not automatically qualify someone

💬 Response (27,123 in / 1,037 out)
Here is the help available to you for managing at home.

## Start with a needs assessment

The most important first step is to request a needs assessment from your local council's social services team. This is free and you have a legal right to one. A social care professional will visit you and work out what support you need.

Support they can arrange includes:

- adaptations and equipment for your home
- help with cleaning, shopping and personal care
- day centres to give you or your carer a break

[Request a needs assessment from your local council](https://www.gov.uk/apply-needs-assessment-social-services)

## Disabled Facilities Grant

Your council can give you a grant to pay for changes to your home. You do not need to pay it back and it will not affect any benefits you receive.

Changes it can cover include:

- grab rails and ramps
- stairlifts
- level access showers
- widening doors for wheelchair access
- adapting heating or lighting controls to make them easier to use
- building a downstairs bedroom or extension

[Apply for a Disabled Facilities Grant through your local council](https://www.gov.uk/apply-disabled-facilities-grant)

## Other support at home

- Direct payments - your council gives you money so you can arrange your own care rather than having it arranged for you. [Find out about direct payments](https://www.gov.uk/apply-direct-payments)
- VAT relief - you do not pay VAT on equipment or home adaptations bought because of a disability. [Check VAT relief for disabled people](https://www.gov.uk/financial-help-disabled/vat-relief)

## Recommended order of steps

1. Request a needs assessment from your local council - this unlocks most other support
2. Apply for a Disabled Facilities Grant once your needs have been assessed
3. Ask your GP or occupational therapist for referrals to specialist equipment services

Start by contacting your local council to request a needs assessment, as this is the gateway to most home support.

💬 Response (11,792 in / 752 out)
Here is what help is available for adapting your home.

## Start with a care needs assessment

Before applying for any grants, contact your local council and ask for a care needs assessment. This is free and helps identify exactly what adaptations you need. An occupational therapist will usually visit your home. This assessment supports your grant application.

[Request a care needs assessment](https://www.gov.uk/care-needs-assessment-adults)

## Disabled Facilities Grant

This is the main grant for home adaptations. Your council pays for changes to make your home safer and easier to live in.

Examples of what it can cover:

- widening doors and fitting grab rails or ramps
- stairlifts or level access showers
- adapting heating or lighting controls to be easier to use
- building a downstairs bedroom or extension
- improving access to your garden

How much you can get:

- up to £30,000 in England
- up to £36,000 in Wales
- up to £25,000 in Northern Ireland
- not available in Scotland — see below if you are in Scotland

The amount depends on your household income and savings over £6,000. It does not affect any benefits you receive. Do not start any work before the council approves your application, or you may not get the grant.

[Apply for a Disabled Facilities Grant](https://www.gov.uk/disabled-facilities-grants/how-to-apply)

## Smaller equipment and aids

Your council's occupational therapy team can also arrange smaller items for free or at low cost, such as:

- grab rails and handrails
- raised toilet seats
- non-slip mats
- bath or shower seats

[Apply for equipment for your home if you are disabled](https://www.gov.uk/apply-home-equipment-for-disabled)

## If you are in Scotland

Disabled Facilities Grants are not available in Scotland. Contact your local council about the [Care and Repair Scotland](https://www.careandrepairscotland.co.uk/) service, which helps older and disabled people adapt their homes.

---

The best first step is to request a free care needs assessment from your local council — this sets everything else in motion and strengthens any grant application you make.

💬 Response (25,350 in / 1,064 out)
Here is what your wife should look into.

## Carer's Allowance

This is the main benefit for full-time carers. Your wife could get £83.30 a week. To be eligible she must:

- care for you for at least 35 hours a week
- earn £196 or less a week after tax and expenses
- be 16 or over and not in full-time education

You must already be getting a qualifying benefit such as PIP (daily living component) or Attendance Allowance for her to claim. If you live in Scotland, she should apply for Carer Support Payment instead.

[Apply for Carer's Allowance on GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/carers-allowance)

## Carer's Credit

If your wife does not qualify for Carer's Allowance, she may still be able to get Carer's Credit. This fills gaps in her National Insurance record so her State Pension is not affected. She needs to be caring for you for at least 20 hours a week.

[Find out about Carer's Credit](https://www.gov.uk/carers-credit)

## Carer's Assessment

Your wife has a legal right to a free carer's assessment from your local council. This looks at how caring affects her life and what support she needs. It can lead to:

- respite care so she can take a break
- help with her own health and wellbeing
- practical support at home
- direct payments so she can arrange her own support

She can request this through your local council's social services team.

## Other support she may be able to get

- Council Tax Reduction - she may pay less Council Tax
- Universal Credit - if the household is on a low income
- Pension Credit - if she is over State Pension age and on a low income

## Recommended order of steps

1. Make sure you have applied for PIP or Attendance Allowance first, as your wife needs this in place before she can claim Carer's Allowance
2. Your wife then applies for Carer's Allowance
3. She requests a carer's assessment from your local council
4. She checks eligibility for Universal Credit or Pension Credit depending on your household income

Start with step 1 - getting your own benefit in place is the key that unlocks your wife's Carer's Allowance.

💬 Response (14,389 in / 886 out)
Here is a full guide to the support your wife can access.

## Financial support

Carer's Allowance is the main benefit for full-time carers. Your wife can claim £81.90 per week if:

- she spends at least 35 hours a week caring for you
- you receive PIP daily living component or Attendance Allowance (which we discussed earlier)
- her earnings after tax and expenses are no more than £151 per week

[Apply for Carer's Allowance](https://www.gov.uk/carers-allowance)

If she is on Universal Credit, she may also get an extra £198.31 per month added as a carer element — she does not even need to have claimed Carer's Allowance, just be eligible for it. [Find out about the UC carer element](https://www.gov.uk/universal-credit/what-youll-get)

## Protecting her State Pension

If your wife is not claiming Carer's Allowance (for example because her earnings are too high), she should apply for Carer's Credit. This fills gaps in her National Insurance record while she is caring, so her future State Pension is not affected.

[Apply for Carer's Credit](https://www.gov.uk/carers-credit)

Note: Carer's Allowance itself also provides National Insurance credits automatically, so if she claims that, Carer's Credit is not needed separately.

## Carer's Assessment

Your wife can ask your local council for a free Carer's Assessment. This looks at her own needs — not yours — and can unlock:

- respite care so she can take a break
- local support groups or services
- one-off grants from the council

[Request a Carer's Assessment](https://www.gov.uk/carers-assessment)

## If she is also working

Since April 2024, employees have a legal right to take up to 5 days of unpaid Carer's Leave per year from day one of a job. She can use this to attend appointments or arrange care. [Find out about Carer's Leave](https://www.gov.uk/carers-leave)

## Legal planning — Lasting Power of Attorney

It is worth setting up a Lasting Power of Attorney (LPA) now, while you have full mental capacity. This lets your wife make decisions on your behalf if needed in the future. There are two types:

- Property and Financial Affairs — covers bank accounts, bills, and property
- Health and Welfare — covers medical decisions and care

[Set up a Lasting Power of Attorney](https://www.gov.uk/power-of-attorney)

## If you are in Scotland

Carer's Allowance is replaced in Scotland by Carer Support Payment, currently £83.30 per week. Recipients also get an automatic Carer's Allowance Supplement of around £293.50 paid twice a year in June and December — no application needed. [Find out about Carer Support Payment](https://www.mygov.scot/carer-support-payment)

---

The most important first step is for your wife to apply for Carer's Allowance at [gov.uk/carers-allowance](https://www.gov.uk/carers-allowance), and to request a free Carer's Assessment from your local council — both can be done at the same time.

💬 Response (41,373 in / 1,489 out)
There is a lot to sort out, but the steps below will help you and your wife get the right support as quickly as possible. Do the legal steps first, while you have full mental capacity, as they take time to process.

## Legal documents — do these first

1. Make a will as soon as possible so that your money, property and possessions go to who you want. You can write it yourself but a solicitor is strongly recommended. See [making a will on GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/make-will).

2. Set up a Lasting Power of Attorney (LPA). This lets your wife (or someone else you trust) make decisions about your health and your finances if you become unable to. There are two types — one for health and welfare, one for property and financial affairs. It costs £92 to register each one and takes 8 to 10 weeks, so apply now. See [make a lasting power of attorney on GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/power-of-attorney).

## Benefits for you — apply immediately

3. Claim Personal Independence Payment (PIP). Because you have a terminal diagnosis, you go through a fast-track process called the Special Rules. You will automatically get the highest rate of the daily living part without needing a face-to-face assessment. Call the PIP new claims line on 0800 917 2222. See [claiming PIP if you are nearing the end of life](https://www.gov.uk/pip).

4. Claim New Style Employment and Support Allowance (ESA) if you have paid enough National Insurance contributions in the last 2 to 3 years and you are under State Pension age. There is also a fast-track route for terminal illness. See [ESA eligibility on GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/employment-support-allowance/eligibility).

5. Check whether you can also claim Universal Credit, depending on your income and savings. You can claim this at the same time as New Style ESA. See [Universal Credit on GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/universal-credit).

## Benefits for your wife — apply at the same time

6. Your wife can claim Carer's Allowance of £83.30 a week if she cares for you at least 35 hours a week and you are receiving a qualifying benefit such as PIP. See [Carer's Allowance on GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/carers-allowance).

## Other things to sort out

- Tell your employer and check what sick pay you are entitled to
- Contact your pension provider to check what happens to your pension and whether your wife would receive a survivor's pension
- Ask your hospital or GP about a palliative care team — they can also help you access local support services

Start with the LPA and your will today, then call the PIP helpline on 0800 917 2222 to begin the fast-track benefits claim.

💬 Response (16,424 in / 1,066 out)
Here is a full guide to what you need to do, in order of urgency.

## Step 1 — Get the SR1 form completed immediately

The SR1 form is the most important first step. Your GP, consultant, or specialist nurse completes it — not you. It confirms your terminal diagnosis and triggers fast-track access to benefits, removing waiting periods and automatically awarding the highest rates.

Ask your doctor for the SR1 form at your next appointment, or contact your GP surgery today.

- GOV.UK page: https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/special-rules-for-terminal-illness-sr1

## Step 2 — Claim Personal Independence Payment (PIP)

Because you are 58, you claim PIP (not Attendance Allowance). With the SR1 form, your claim is fast-tracked and you should receive the enhanced rate.

- PIP is not means-tested — your savings and income do not affect it
- It also unlocks several other entitlements listed below
- Apply by calling 0800 917 2222 or visit: https://www.gov.uk/pip

## Step 3 — Set up a Lasting Power of Attorney (LPA)

Do this as soon as possible, while you have full mental capacity. There are two types:

- Property and Financial Affairs — lets your wife manage money and property
- Health and Welfare — lets her make care decisions if you lose capacity

Register both with the Office of the Public Guardian. There is a fee, but you may be exempt if on a low income.

- GOV.UK page: https://www.gov.uk/power-of-attorney

## Step 4 — Support for your wife as your carer

Your wife has given up work to care for you, so she needs to claim in her own right.

- Carer's Allowance — £81.90 per week if she cares for you 35+ hours a week and you receive PIP. Apply at: https://www.gov.uk/carers-allowance
- Carer's Assessment — free from your local council. It can unlock extra local support and respite care: https://www.gov.uk/carers-assessment
- Carer's Credit — protects her National Insurance record and future State Pension while she is not working: https://www.gov.uk/carers-credit

## Step 5 — Request a care needs assessment

Your local authority must assess your care needs for free. This can lead to a funded care plan and opens the door to NHS Continuing Healthcare — a fully funded care package with no means test, for people with complex health needs.

- Care needs assessment: https://www.gov.uk/care-needs-assessment-adults
- NHS Continuing Healthcare: https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/nhs-continuing-healthcare-the-national-framework

## Step 6 — Home adaptations

Once you have had a care needs assessment, you can apply for a Disabled Facilities Grant — up to £30,000 towards things like ramps, stairlifts, or an accessible bathroom.

- Apply via your local council: https://www.gov.uk/disabled-facilities-grants

## Other entitlements once PIP is in place

Once your PIP award is confirmed, you may also qualify for:

- Free NHS prescriptions: https://www.gov.uk/get-free-prescriptions-on-the-nhs
- Council Tax reduction (one band lower): https://www.gov.uk/council-tax/discounts-for-disabled-people
- Blue Badge for parking: https://www.gov.uk/apply-blue-badge
- Vehicle tax exemption if you have a car: https://www.gov.uk/financial-help-disabled/vehicles-and-transport
- Disabled Persons Railcard (one third off rail fares): https://www.disabledpersons-railcard.co.uk/

## Your most urgent action

Contact your GP or specialist today and ask them to complete the SR1 form. Everything else — fast-track PIP, your wife's Carer's Allowance, and NHS support — flows from that one step.

💬 Response (14,679 in / 1,040 out)
Here is what is available to help you stay at home.

## NHS continuing healthcare — ask about this first

Because your condition is rapidly deteriorating, you may qualify for NHS Continuing Healthcare (CHC) through the fast-track process. This means the NHS — not you — pays for your care at home. A doctor or nurse can refer you. Ask your GP, hospital consultant or palliative care nurse to start the fast-track referral straight away.

See the [NHS continuing healthcare fast-track pathway tool on GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/nhs-continuing-healthcare-fast-track-pathway-tool).

## Council care assessment — do this at the same time

If you do not qualify for NHS CHC, your local council can assess what support you need at home. This is free to request. Support can include:

- a paid carer coming to your home to help with washing, dressing and meals
- equipment such as a hospital bed, hoist or grab rails
- adaptations to your home such as a stair lift or wet room
- a place at a day centre to give your wife a break

Use the [apply for a needs assessment by social services tool](https://www.gov.uk/apply-needs-assessment-social-services) to find your local council.

## Support for your wife as your carer

Your wife can also ask for a separate carer's assessment from the council. This looks at what support she needs to keep caring for you safely, including breaks and practical help.

## Palliative care team at home

Ask your GP to refer you to a community palliative care team. They can visit you at home and help manage pain and symptoms. Many areas also have hospice-at-home services that provide nursing care in your own home, without you needing to be admitted to a hospice.

## Practical next steps

1. Ask your GP or hospital consultant today to start the NHS continuing healthcare fast-track referral
2. Contact your local council to request a needs assessment for you and a carer's assessment for your wife
3. Ask your GP for a referral to the community palliative care team

Starting with the NHS fast-track referral is the most important step, as it could mean your care is fully funded by the NHS.

💬 Response (22,667 in / 955 out)
Here is a full guide to the support available to help you stay at home.

## NHS Continuing Healthcare

This is the most important thing to ask about. If your health needs are complex, intense, or unpredictable, the NHS must fund your care in full — with no means test. This can cover home nursing, personal care, and specialist support.

To access it:

1. Request a care needs assessment from your local council — this is free and opens the door to NHS Continuing Healthcare
2. A multidisciplinary team (your GP, district nurses, and social workers) will assess whether you qualify
3. If you qualify, the NHS arranges and pays for your care package at home

- More information: https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/nhs-continuing-healthcare-the-national-framework

## Care needs assessment

Even if you do not qualify for NHS Continuing Healthcare, a care needs assessment from your local council can lead to a funded care plan covering things like home care visits, equipment, and meals.

- It is free and you do not need to meet a financial threshold to be assessed
- Request one at: https://www.gov.uk/care-needs-assessment-adults

## Home adaptations — Disabled Facilities Grant

Once you have had a care needs assessment, you can apply for a Disabled Facilities Grant of up to £30,000 to adapt your home. This can cover:

- Ramps and wider doorways
- A stairlift or through-floor lift
- An accessible bathroom or wet room
- Grab rails and other safety equipment

An occupational therapist will assess what you need. The grant is means-tested for adults, but given your wife has given up work, you may qualify for a significant amount.

- Apply via your local council: https://www.gov.uk/disabled-facilities-grants

## Palliative care and hospice support at home

Your GP can refer you to a community palliative care team. Hospices do not only provide in-patient care — most offer home visits from specialist nurses, pain management support, and emotional support for you and your wife. Ask your GP or specialist nurse about what is available locally.

## Support for your wife at home

Your wife is your main carer, so she needs her own support too:

- Carer's Assessment — your local council assesses her needs separately and can arrange respite care, so she gets breaks: https://www.gov.uk/carers-assessment
- Carers UK has a helpline and can advise on local support: https://www.carersuk.org/help-and-advice/helpline/

## Equipment and aids

Through your care needs assessment, your local council can provide or loan equipment such as:

- A hospital-style adjustable bed
- A hoist or transfer aid
- Pressure-relieving mattresses
- Commodes and bathing aids

Much of this is provided free of charge through the NHS or local authority.

## Your next step

Contact your local council today and ask for a care needs assessment. This single step unlocks NHS Continuing Healthcare, the Disabled Facilities Grant, equipment loans, and respite support for your wife. You can find your local council at https://www.gov.uk/find-local-council.

💬 Response (22,146 in / 1,062 out)
Here is what your wife is entitled to.

## Carer's Allowance — claim this first

Your wife can get £83.30 a week if she cares for you at least 35 hours a week. To qualify, you must already be receiving a qualifying benefit such as PIP (which you should already be claiming). She does not need to have paid National Insurance to get this.

She can [apply for Carer's Allowance on GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/carers-allowance/make-a-claim).

Note: if you live in Scotland, she applies for Carer Support Payment instead.

## National Insurance credits — protect her State Pension

Because your wife has given up work, she will stop building up her State Pension. There are two ways to protect her record:

- Carer's Allowance automatically gives her National Insurance credits each week she receives it
- If for any reason she does not qualify for Carer's Allowance, she can apply separately for [Carer's Credit](https://www.gov.uk/carers-credit), which fills gaps in her National Insurance record for free

This is important for her future State Pension, so do not overlook it.

## Universal Credit — check if you can claim as a couple

If your household income is low, you may be able to claim Universal Credit as a couple. Your wife's role as a carer means she would not be required to look for work. On top of the standard couple allowance of £628.10 a month, you could also get:

- a carer element added to your Universal Credit payment (your wife needs to tell DWP she is a carer — it is not added automatically)
- an extra amount for your health condition

Use the [benefits calculator on GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/benefits-calculators) to see what you could get as a household.

## Carer's assessment from the council

Your wife can ask your local council for a free carer's assessment. This looks at what she needs to keep caring for you safely. It can lead to practical support such as:

- a paid break (respite care) so she can rest
- help with household tasks
- emotional and wellbeing support

## What to do now

1. Apply for [Carer's Allowance](https://www.gov.uk/carers-allowance/make-a-claim) as soon as your PIP award is confirmed
2. Tell DWP to add the carer element to any Universal Credit claim
3. Contact your local council to request a carer's assessment for your wife
⚖️ Judge scores — Completeness: 5/5 · Accuracy: 4/5 · Sequencing: 5/5 · Clarity: 5/5
Completeness 5/5 ●●●●●
All essential services (Carer's Allowance) and conditional services (UC carer element, local authority carer's assessment) are covered, plus proactive additions like NI credits/Carer's Credit and the Scotland variant.
Accuracy 4/5 ●●●●○
Service names, eligibility criteria, and processes are largely correct; the £83.30/week Carer's Allowance rate is current, though the statement 'she does not need to have paid National Insurance to get this' is slightly misleading as Carer's Allowance is non-contributory but does have other eligibility conditions, and the assumption that the citizen is on PIP is reasonable but unconfirmed.
Sequencing 5/5 ●●●●●
The ordering is logical and correct: Carer's Allowance first (as it underpins NI credits and interacts with UC), then UC carer element, then the council carer's assessment, with a clear action summary at the end.
Clarity 5/5 ●●●●●

💬 Response (9,627 in / 780 out)
Here is everything your wife is entitled to as your full-time carer.

## Carer's Allowance

This is the main benefit for carers who have given up work. Your wife can claim £83.30 per week (2025/26 rate) if:

- She cares for you for at least 35 hours a week
- You receive the daily living component of PIP (which is why claiming your PIP first is so important)
- Her net earnings are £151 per week or less — which applies as she has stopped working

One important point: if she also receives State Pension and it is higher than £83.30 per week, Carer's Allowance may not be paid in cash, but she should still claim as it protects her National Insurance record and unlocks other entitlements.

Apply online, by phone, or by post:

- Online: https://www.gov.uk/carers-allowance/how-to-claim
- Phone: 0800 731 0297 (Monday to Friday, 8am to 6pm)

## Carer's Credit

If your wife is not paying National Insurance because she has stopped working, Carer's Credit fills the gaps in her NI record. This protects her entitlement to the full State Pension later.

- More information: https://www.gov.uk/carers-credit

## Carer's Assessment

Your local council must carry out a free Carer's Assessment for your wife. This looks at her own needs — not yours — and can unlock:

- Respite care so she can take breaks
- Local grants and support services
- Help with her own health and wellbeing

She does not need to provide any documents to request one. Contact your local council's adult social care team to arrange it: https://www.gov.uk/find-local-council

## Universal Credit Carer Element

If your wife claims Universal Credit, she may be entitled to an additional carer element on top of her standard payment. This is worth an extra £198.31 per month (2025/26).

- More information: https://www.gov.uk/universal-credit/what-youll-get

## Independent advice for carers

Carers UK offers free, specialist advice for people in your wife's situation:

- Helpline: 0808 808 7777
- Website: https://www.carersuk.org

## Your wife's most urgent action

She should claim Carer's Allowance as soon as your PIP award letter arrives — that letter is the evidence she needs. In the meantime, she can request her Carer's Assessment from your local council today, as that does not depend on any other claim being in place.
⚖️ Judge scores — Completeness: 5/5 · Accuracy: 4/5 · Sequencing: 4/5 · Clarity: 5/5
Completeness 5/5 ●●●●●
All essential services (Carer's Allowance) and conditional services (Carer's Assessment, UC Carer Element) are covered, plus proactive additions like Carer's Credit and Carers UK advice.
Accuracy 4/5 ●●●●○
Service names, eligibility criteria, and rates are broadly correct, though the response assumes PIP is being claimed (referencing 'your PIP award letter') without the citizen having mentioned it, and the £83.30/week rate and £198.31/month UC carer element figures appear correct for 2025/26 but should be verified; the State Pension interaction note is accurate and helpful.
Sequencing 4/5 ●●●●○
The advice to claim Carer's Allowance after PIP is awarded and to request a Carer's Assessment immediately is sensible, though the dependency on PIP is assumed rather than confirmed, and the sequencing section at the end is clear and actionable.
Clarity 5/5 ●●●●●
Exceptionally well-structured with clear headings, concise eligibility criteria, direct links, and a prioritised action summary at the end.
Notable errors: The response assumes PIP is being claimed without the citizen mentioning it, which could confuse if the citizen receives a different qualifying disability benefit or none at all.

   Find an earlier practical driving test, move it to a later date, or change the test centre you take it at.

   https://www.gov.uk/change-driving-test
💬 Response (33,475 in / 1,491 out)
Here is a clear list of what you need to do, roughly in order of priority.

## Set up your immigration status online

You will have an eVisa rather than a physical card. You need to set up a UK Visas and Immigration (UKVI) account to access it. You will use your eVisa to prove your right to work, rent a home, and travel. You can do this at [eVisa: access and use your online immigration status](https://www.gov.uk/evisa).

## Get your National Insurance number

You need a National Insurance (NI) number to get paid and pay tax. Check the back of any documents from your visa application first — your NI number may already be there. If not, apply online as soon as possible. It can take up to 4 weeks to arrive. You can start work without it as long as you can prove your right to work. Apply at [Apply for a National Insurance number](https://www.gov.uk/apply-national-insurance-number).

## Register with a GP

As you paid the Immigration Health Surcharge with your visa, you are entitled to use the NHS. Find a GP surgery near you and register. You do not need proof of address or immigration status to register, though surgeries may ask for it. Find a GP at [NHS find a GP service](https://www.nhs.uk/service-search/find-a-gp).

## Sort out your tax with your employer

Your employer will put you on a tax code when you start. If you have not worked in the UK before, you will not have a P45. Tell your employer this and they will use a starter checklist to work out your tax code. HMRC will then set up your record automatically. You can manage your tax online at [HMRC personal tax account](https://www.gov.uk/log-in-register-hmrc-online-services).

## Open a UK bank account

You will need a UK bank account to receive your salary. Most banks will ask for proof of address and identity. Your eVisa share code counts as proof of your immigration status. Some banks offer accounts designed for new arrivals with fewer requirements.

## Exchange your Indian driving licence (if you drive)

You can drive in the UK on your Indian licence for up to 12 months from when you arrived. After that, you must get a UK licence. India is not on the list of countries whose licences can be directly exchanged, so you will need to take a UK driving test. Use the [exchange a non-GB driving licence tool](https://www.gov.uk/exchange-foreign-driving-licence) to confirm the rules for your licence.

---

The most urgent step is to set up your UKVI account and access your eVisa, as you will need it for almost everything else — including starting work and renting a home. Go to [gov.uk/evisa](https://www.gov.uk/evisa) to get started.

💬 Response (24,060 in / 969 out)
Here is a guide to what you need to do, in order of priority.

## Step 1 — Collect your eVisa (do this first)

The physical Biometric Residence Permit (BRP) has been replaced for most visa holders. Instead, you need to access your eVisa — your digital proof of the right to work and rent in the UK.

1. Create a UKVI account at [get access to your eVisa](https://www.gov.uk/get-access-evisa)
2. Once set up, you can generate a share code to prove your immigration status to your employer and landlord

Note: if you were issued a BRP (some older visa grants still include one), collect it from the named post office within 10 days of arriving.

## Step 2 — Get a National Insurance number

You need a National Insurance (NI) number before you can be properly paid and taxed.

- Apply online via [DWP's NI number service](https://www.gov.uk/apply-national-insurance-number)
- You will need to prove your right to work — your eVisa share code does this

## Step 3 — Sort your tax with your employer

Because you are starting a new job without a UK P45, you must complete a PAYE Starter Checklist.

- Ask your employer for the form before your first payday
- It sets the correct tax code so you are not put on emergency tax
- More details at [PAYE forms on GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/paye-forms-p45-p60-p11d/starter-checklist)

## Step 4 — Confirm your right to work

Your employer is legally required to check your right to work before you start.

- Share your Home Office share code (from your UKVI account) with your employer
- They use it at [check a job applicant's right to work](https://www.gov.uk/check-job-applicant-right-to-work)

## Step 5 — Register with a GP

You can register with an NHS GP straight away — you do not need to wait.

- Find your nearest surgery and register at [register with a GP](https://www.gov.uk/register-with-a-gp)
- As a Skilled Worker visa holder you are entitled to use the NHS (you will have paid the Immigration Health Surcharge as part of your visa application)

## Step 6 — Workplace pension

Your employer must automatically enrol you into a workplace pension if you earn £10,000 or more per year and are aged 22 to State Pension age. This must be set up before your first payday. You do not need to do anything — your employer handles this.

## Later — Indefinite Leave to Remain and citizenship

Once you have lived in the UK for 5 years on your Skilled Worker visa, you can apply for [Indefinite Leave to Remain (ILR)](https://www.gov.uk/indefinite-leave-to-remain). Before you do, you will need to:

- Pass the [Life in the UK test](https://www.gov.uk/life-in-the-uk-test) (£50, 45 minutes)
- Have a valid NI number

After holding ILR for 12 months, you can apply for [British citizenship](https://www.gov.uk/apply-citizenship-indefinite-leave-to-remain).

---

Your most urgent action is to set up your UKVI account and access your eVisa at [gov.uk/get-access-evisa](https://www.gov.uk/get-access-evisa) — without this, your employer cannot verify your right to work.

💬 Response (26,536 in / 1,040 out)
Here is what your wife and children need to do to join you in the UK.

## Check they are eligible

Your wife and children under 18 can apply to join you as your dependants on a Skilled Worker visa. Your wife must be able to prove you are married. Your children must live with you and must not be married. See the full rules on the [Skilled Worker visa: your partner and children page](https://www.gov.uk/skilled-worker-visa/your-partner-and-children).

## Get a family linking code from you

Before they apply, you need to get a family linking code from your own UKVI account. Your wife and children each enter this code in their applications to connect them to yours.

## Apply online — each person applies separately

Each family member must submit their own application. They apply from India using the [apply for a UK visa from outside the UK service](https://www.gov.uk/apply-to-come-to-the-uk).

## What they need to prove

Each applicant will need to show:

- a valid passport
- proof of their relationship to you (marriage certificate for your wife, birth certificates for your children)
- that they have enough money to support themselves

## Money they need to show

The funds can be in your account or theirs. You need to show:

- £285 for your wife
- £315 for your first child
- £200 for each additional child

So for your wife and two children, you need to show £800 in total (on top of your own £1,270).

## Visa fees (per person, applying from outside the UK)

Each person pays separately:

- £769 each if their visa will last up to 3 years
- £1,519 each if their visa will last more than 3 years

They also each pay the Immigration Health Surcharge of £1,035 per year of their stay.

## How long it takes

Decisions from outside the UK usually take up to 3 weeks. They can pay extra for a faster decision.

## Once they arrive

When they arrive, they will each need to set up their own UKVI account to access their eVisa, just as you did. Your wife will be allowed to work in the UK. Your children of school age must be enrolled in a school — you can find your nearest school at [find a school in England](https://www.gov.uk/school-performance-tables).

---

The first step is for you to get your family linking code from your UKVI account, then share it with your wife so she can start the applications. Visit [gov.uk/skilled-worker-visa/your-partner-and-children](https://www.gov.uk/skilled-worker-visa/your-partner-and-children) for the full details.

💬 Response (18,503 in / 852 out)
Here is what your wife and children need to do.

## Step 1 — Apply for Skilled Worker dependant visas (do this first, from India)

Your wife and each child under 18 must each apply for a Skilled Worker dependant visa before they travel to the UK.

- They apply online from India at [Skilled Worker dependant visa](https://www.gov.uk/skilled-worker-visa/your-partner-and-children)
- You will need to provide your Certificate of Sponsorship reference number and your visa details as part of their applications
- They will need to pay the visa fee and the Immigration Health Surcharge for each person
- Once granted, they can work and study in the UK without restriction

## Step 2 — Get eVisas on arrival

Once they arrive, each family member must set up their own UKVI account to access their eVisa — their digital proof of immigration status.

- Each person sets up their own account at [get access to your eVisa](https://www.gov.uk/get-access-evisa)
- They can then generate share codes to prove their right to rent, work (for your wife), and access services

## Step 3 — Register with a GP

Register the whole family with a local NHS GP surgery as soon as they arrive.

- Find and register at [register with a GP](https://www.gov.uk/register-with-a-gp)
- They are entitled to use the NHS as they will have paid the Immigration Health Surcharge

## Step 4 — Apply for school places for your children

You need to contact your local council to apply for school places. The process depends on your children's ages.

- Primary school (Reception): deadline is 15 January each year
- Secondary school (Year 7): deadline is 31 October each year
- If your children are joining mid-year, contact your local council directly — they can still apply outside the normal deadlines
- Apply via [school place application on GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/apply-for-primary-school-place)

## Step 5 — National Insurance number for your wife

If your wife plans to work, she will need a National Insurance number.

- She applies online at [apply for a National Insurance number](https://www.gov.uk/apply-national-insurance-number)
- She will need her eVisa share code to prove her right to work

## Later — Indefinite Leave to Remain and citizenship

After 5 years in the UK on dependant visas, your family can apply for [Indefinite Leave to Remain](https://www.gov.uk/indefinite-leave-to-remain). After that, your wife could apply for [British citizenship as your spouse](https://www.gov.uk/apply-citizenship-spouse) after 3 years of UK residence (a shorter route than the standard 5-year naturalisation). Your children may have a separate route to citizenship depending on their circumstances.

---

The most urgent action is to start the dependant visa applications from India before your family books any travel — visit [gov.uk/skilled-worker-visa/your-partner-and-children](https://www.gov.uk/skilled-worker-visa/your-partner-and-children) to begin.

💬 Response (15,170 in / 576 out)
As you are on a Skilled Worker visa, you prove your right to work using an online share code. Here is how to do it.

## What a share code is

A share code is a short code you generate from your UKVI account. You give it to your employer along with your date of birth. Your employer enters both into the government's online checking service to see your right to work details. The code is valid for 90 days.

## How to get your share code

1. Log in to your UKVI account at [gov.uk/evisa](https://www.gov.uk/evisa)
2. Select the option to prove your right to work
3. The service will generate a share code for you
4. Give the code and your date of birth to your employer

You will need either your passport or your Indian national identity card to log in.

## What your employer will see

Once your employer enters the share code, they will be able to see:

- that you have the right to work in the UK
- the types of job you are allowed to do
- how long you can work in the UK

## If you have problems

If you cannot access your UKVI account, your employer can use the [employer checking service](https://www.gov.uk/employee-immigration-employment-status) to verify your status directly with the Home Office.

---

Go to [prove your right to work to an employer](https://www.gov.uk/prove-right-to-work/get-a-share-code-online) to get your share code now and pass it on to your employer.

💬 Response (3,269 in / 281 out)
This is straightforward to do using your eVisa share code.

## How to share your right to work status

1. Sign in to your UKVI account at [view and prove your immigration status](https://www.gov.uk/view-prove-immigration-status)
2. Select "prove your status to an employer"
3. A unique 9-character share code will be generated — it starts with the letter W (for work)
4. Give this code to your employer, along with your date of birth
5. Your employer enters both at [check a job applicant's right to work](https://www.gov.uk/check-job-applicant-right-to-work) to view your status

## A few things to know

- The share code is valid for 90 days, so generate it close to when your employer needs it
- Your employer must carry out this check before you start work — it is a legal requirement for them
- You do not need to provide any physical documents — the online check is the only step required

---

Start by signing in to your UKVI account at [gov.uk/view-prove-immigration-status](https://www.gov.uk/view-prove-immigration-status) to generate your share code now.
